House releases an image of Mr Trump signing the new executive order</p></div></figcaption></figure></div><div class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><b class="ssrcss-1xjjfut-BoldText e5tfeyi3">President Donald Trump has signed a new executive order placing a 90-day ban on people from six mainly Muslim nations.</b></p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Iraq - which was covered in the previous seven-nation order - has been removed from the new one after agreeing to additional visa vetting measures.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10"><a class="ssrcss-f6h2dj-InlineLink e1kn3p7n0" href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2017/03/06/executive-order-protecting-nation-foreign-terrorist-entry-united-states">The directive<span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">, <!-- -->external</span></a>, which includes a 120-day ban on all refugees, takes effect on 16 March. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The previous order, which was blocked by a federal court, sparked confusion at airports and mass protests.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Presented as a means to strengthen national security against terror threats, it was blocked by the courts and effectively remains on hold.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The new order was unveiled by Secretary of State Rex Tillerson, Attorney General Jeff Sessions and Department of Homeland Security Secretary John Kelly.</p></div></div><div class="ssrcss-10wcwg8-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1" class="ssrcss-1o1fzgd-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0" data-component="subheadline-block"><h2 class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0" id="What-is-different-about-the-new-order" tabindex="-1"><span role="text">What is different about the new order?</span></h2></div><div class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Citizens of Iran, Libya, Syria, Somalia, Sudan and Yemen, the other six countries on the original 27 January order, will once more be subject to a 90-day travel ban.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Iraq has been taken off the banned list because its government has boosted visa screening and data sharing, White House officials said. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The new directive says refugees already approved by the State Department can enter the US. It also lifts an indefinite ban on all Syrian refugees. </p></div></div><div class="ssrcss-10wcwg8-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1" data-component="image-block"><figure class="ssrcss-12gl1u2-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-5zsoxt-Placeholder etlorgc0"><picture><source srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 320w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/480/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 480w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/624/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 624w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/800/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 800w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/976/cpsprodpb/ABBD/production/_94956934_d25b9109-348e-45b4-ad8e-4bc4885e3739.jpg.webp 976w" type="image/webp"/><img alt="Iraqi immigrant Hameed Darwish addresses the media after being released from Terminal 4 at John F. class="ssrcss-bm8gf8-StyledFigureCaption ehbdhz00"><span class="visually-hidden ssrcss-1f39n02-VisuallyHidden e16en2lz0">Image caption, </span><div class="ssrcss-1ml6m0y-Stack e1y4nx260" reports</p></div></figcaption></figure></div><div class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Green Card holders (legal permanent residents of the US) from the named countries will not be affected.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The new order does not give priority to religious minorities, unlike the previous directive. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Critics of the Trump administration had argued that this was an unlawful policy showing preference to Christian refugees.</p></div></div><div class="ssrcss-10wcwg8-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1" data-component="image-block"><figure </span><div class="ssrcss-1ml6m0y-Stack e1y4nx260" spacing="6"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Rex Tillerson: "President Trump is exercising his rightful authority to keep our people safe"</p></div></figcaption></figure></div><div class="ssrcss-1o1fzgd-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0" data-component="subheadline-block"><h2 class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0" id="What-does-the-administration-say" tabindex="-1"><span role="text">What does the administration say?</span></h2></div><div class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The three Cabinet secretaries held a joint news conference on Monday morning to discuss the new directive. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">America's top US diplomat said the order was meant to "eliminate vulnerabilities that radical Islamic terrorists can and will exploit for destructive ends".</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Mr Sessions said that, according to the FBI, more than 300 people who entered the US as refugees are under investigation for potential terrorism-related offences. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The top US prosecutor said three of the countries were state sponsors of terrorism.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The other three, Mr Sessions said, had lost control of territory to militants such as the Islamic State group or al-Qaeda. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Mr Kelly added that unregulated and unvetted travel was putting national security at risk. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">He said the US cannot tolerate "malevolent actors using our immigration system to take American lives". </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">None of the cabinet secretaries took any questions after the press conference.</p></div></div><div class="ssrcss-10wcwg8-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1" data-component="image-block"><figure class="ssrcss-12gl1u2-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-ciorxc-Placeholder etlorgc0"><picture><source srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/7F16/production/_92443523_464x2.jpg.webp 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/7F16/production/_92443523_464x2.jpg.webp 320w" type="image/webp"/><img alt="Grey line" class="ssrcss-11yxrdo-Image edrdn950" height="2" loading="lazy" src="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/464/cpsprodpb/7F16/production/_92443523_464x2.jpg" srcset="https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/240/cpsprodpb/7F16/production/_92443523_464x2.jpg 240w, https://ichef.bbci.co.uk/ace/standard/320/cpsprodpb/7F16/production/_92443523_464x2.jpg 320w" width="464"/></picture></span></div></figure></div><div class="ssrcss-1o1fzgd-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0" data-component="subheadline-block"><h2 class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0" id="Analysis-Anthony-Zurcher-BBC-News-Washington-" tabindex="-1"><span role="text">Analysis - Anthony Zurcher, BBC News, Washington </span></h2></div><div class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Donald Trump has, at last, unveiled his new immigration order, and it looks like government lawyers - and not just White House political operatives like Steve Bannon and Stephen Miller - have had their input. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Gone are the most controversial measures of the old order, such as preference for Christian refugees and the suspension of existing visas and green cards. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">The details of the action's implementation are outlined with greater clarity this time, with more than a week before the new rules kick in.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">It's still an open question as to what, if anything, this order will do to prevent violent attacks on US soil, given that past high-profile incidents have not involved individuals from any of the six named countries.</p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Mr Trump had promised bold action on border security, however - the kind of move that would unnerve traditional politicians and anger civil liberties advocates. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Given the early reaction from groups like the ACLU and Democratic leaders, the story is unfolding as expected. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Although Mr Trump's campaign-rally talk of sweeping Muslim bans are a thing of the past, his supporters will likely revel in the uproar and consider this latest move a campaign promise kept. </p></div></div><div class="ssrcss-10wcwg8-ComponentWrapper-FullWidthWrapper ep2nwvo1" data-component="image-block"><figure class="ssrcss-12gl1u2-StyledFigure e34k3c22"><div class="ssrcss-ab5fd8-StyledFigureContainer e34k3c21"><span class="ssrcss-ciorxc-Placeholder class="ssrcss-1o1fzgd-ComponentWrapper-HeadlineComponentWrapper egtrm1f0" data-component="subheadline-block"><h2 class="ssrcss-pbttu9-Heading e10rt3ze0" class="ssrcss-suhx0k-RichTextComponentWrapper ep2nwvo0" data-component="text-block"><div class="ssrcss-1o5p6v2-RichTextContainer e5tfeyi1"><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">Yes. New York Attorney General Eric Schneiderman - the state's highest ranking law enforcement officer - issued a statement on Monday saying his office is ready to take the Trump administration to court. </p><p class="ssrcss-1q0x1qg-Paragraph e1jhz7w10">"While the White House may have made changes to the ban, the intent to discriminate against Muslims remains clear," he said. </p><p
